> *A visual, guided Starship prompt configuration builder*

### Core UX principle
> **The TOML is the truth. The preview is guidance.**

---

## 🧭 New App Structure (3 explicit modes)

### 🔧 Build
> *“I am configuring Starship”*

- Schema‑driven forms only
- Every option:
  - Has a description
  - Shows its TOML key
  - Validates input
- Unsupported options **cannot appear**

✅ No drag, no fluff

---

### 👀 Preview
> *“I want to see roughly how this will look”*

- Visual prompt layout
- Module order
- Colors / spacing (clearly marked *approximate*)
- Banner:
  > ⚠️ Preview is an approximation. Starship controls final rendering.

---

### 📦 Export
> *“Give me something I can use”*

- Read‑only TOML
- Live diff
- Validation warnings
- Copy / Download
- “Test locally” instructions

---

## 🧱 UI Layout (simple & strong)

```
┌───────────────────────────────┐
│ Starship Command Enhanced     │
│ Build | Preview | Export      │
└───────────────────────────────┘

┌────────────┐ ┌─────────────────────────┐
│ Modules    │ │ Module Settings          │
│ ▸ git      │ │ [enabled ✅]              │
│ ▸ nodejs   │ │ symbol = "⬢"              │
│ ▸ time     │ │ format = "[$time]"        │
│            │ │ TOML: [git]               │
└────────────┘ └─────────────────────────┘

┌────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ Live TOML Preview                       │
│ (diff highlighted)                      │
└────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

# 3️⃣ Fancy, Eye‑Catching `README.md` (ready to paste)

```markdown
# 🚀 Starship Command Enhanced

> A visual, guided configuration builder for the  
> **Starship cross‑shell prompt**

./docs/preview.png

---

## ✨ What is this?

Starship Command Enhanced helps you **build a correct, clean `starship.toml`**
without memorizing documentation or guessing which options actually work.

✅ Visual builder  
✅ Live TOML output  
✅ Approximate prompt preview  
✅ Schema‑aware options  
✅ Zero magic — just real config

---

## 🧠 Philosophy

- **The TOML is the source of truth**
- **Preview is guidance, not a promise**
- **If Starship can’t do it, we don’t fake it**

---

## 🔧 How it works

1. Configure modules in **Build**
2. Sanity‑check layout in **Preview**
3. Copy validated config in **Export**
4. Paste into `~/.config/starship.toml`
5. Enjoy ✨

---

## 📦 Features

- Guided module configuration
- Live config diff
- Presets for quick starts
- Inline Starship documentation
- Validation & warnings
- Clean, modern UI

---

## ⚠️ Important Notes

> This app does **not** execute Starship.
> Preview output is an approximation only.

For final appearance, always test locally.

---

## 🛣️ Roadmap

See ./ROADMAP.md

---

## 🤝 Contributing

PRs welcome.
If you’re unsure — open an issue first.

---

## 📜 License

MIT
```

- Agents

## ✅ TOP PRIORITY (Do these first – highest value)

### 1️⃣ **Stop the confusion: split the app into 3 modes**
**Recommendation:**  
Implement **Build / Preview / Export** as explicit modes.

**Why this matters:**  
This instantly explains *what the app is doing* at any moment — even to you.

**Actionable suggestion:**
- Build → real Starship options only
- Preview → approximate visuals, clearly labeled
- Export → validated `starship.toml` only

✅ This alone fixes ~50% of the UX problem.

---

### 2️⃣ **Audit and classify every option**
**Recommendation:**  
Create a rule that every option must be exactly one of:
- ✅ Runtime (written to TOML)
- 👀 Preview‑only
- ❌ Unsupported (remove)

**Why:**  
“Options that do nothing” destroy trust.

**Actionable suggestion:**
- Remove unsupported options immediately
- Label preview‑only options clearly
- If it doesn’t affect TOML, say so

---

### 3️⃣ **Make TOML the visible source of truth**
**Recommendation:**  
Show the generated `starship.toml` **at all times** (or one click away).

**Why:**  
This grounds the user and prevents magical thinking.

**Actionable suggestion:**
- Live TOML pane
- Highlight diffs when options change
- Read‑only, copy‑ready

---

## ✅ SECOND PRIORITY (Big UX gains, still fast)

### 4️⃣ **Add presets to give users context**
**Recommendation:**  
Ship 3–5 presets:
- Minimal
- Developer
- Nerd Font
- Clean

**Why:**  
Blank canvases are confusing. Presets teach usage *implicitly*.

**Actionable suggestion:**
- Presets are just configs, not special logic
- Users can inspect and modify them

---

### 5️⃣ **Tooltips that answer “why does this exist?”**
**Recommendation:**  
Every option gets a tooltip explaining:
- What it changes
- Where it appears in TOML
- Whether it’s preview‑only

**Why:**  
If you can’t explain it, the option shouldn’t exist.

---

## ✅ THIRD PRIORITY (Polish & trust)

### 6️⃣ **Schema‑based validation**
**Recommendation:**  
Validate configs against Starship’s schema.

**Why:**  
Prevents broken exports and increases confidence.

**Actionable suggestion:**
- Warnings, not silent failures
- Highlight unsupported combos

---

### 7️⃣ **Rewrite documentation to explain intent**
**Recommendation:**  
Docs should explain:
- What the app is *for*
- What it intentionally does *not* do
- How preview differs from real Starship output

**Why:**  
Good docs reduce issues and self‑doubt.

---

## ✅ What NOT to do (important)

❌ Don’t add more visual knobs

## 1. User Manual

### 🦄 The Starship Ecosystem

Your environment is a **Tiered Intelligence Mesh** with:
- 374 local skills
- Two primary AI engines

#### 1.1 The Command Hub

- **Gemini CLI**: Local “Commander” agent (Node.js/Termux)
- **Jules CLI**: Remote “Engineer” agent (Google Cloud/PRoot)
- **Skillfish**: Discovery layer (Local/Cache)

#### 1.2 Core Interaction Protocols

- **Slash Commands**: `/pickle`, `/dev:create-prd`, etc.
- **Skill Activation**: On-demand expertise loading
- **Persistent Loops**: Automated task refinement via AfterAgent hooks

> 💡 **Pro Tip**: Activate skills _before_ describing a complex task to maximize token efficiency.

---

## 2. Technical Manual

### 🧊 Architecture & Infrastructure

#### 2.1 The Networking Wall (Android/Termux)

- **DNS Fix**: Forced Go resolver via `env GODEBUG=netdns=go`
- **SSL Fix**: Bind Android CA-certs to standard Linux paths via proot

#### 2.2 The God Mode Wrapper

- Persistent wrapper script at `~/.local/bin/jules`
- Maps environment and simulates a standard Linux filesystem

> 🧠 **Architectural Note**: `proot` creates a user-space simulation, bypassing Android’s restrictions without root access.

---

## 3. Developer Guide

### 👾 Authoring Expertise

#### 3.1 The TDD Skill Workflow

- **RED**: Reproduce a task failure
- **GREEN**: Write minimal `SKILL.md` to define the fix
- **REFACTOR**: Audit for “AI Slop” and token density

#### 3.2 Manifest Schema

- Extensions define boundaries using `excludeTools` to prevent agent conflicts

## 4. Standard Operating Procedures (SOP)

### ⛓️ Agent Chain Protocols

#### SOP-001: The Autonomous PRD Workflow

1. Run `/dev:create-prd "Feature Description"`
2. Review with editorial-audit skill
3. Commit PRD to `docs/` before writing code

#### SOP-002: Scaling Expertise (Skill Injection)

1. Copy skill content to clipboard
2. Start Jules with `jules new "Use this skill logic: [paste content] ... [task instruction]"`

## 10. Accessibility & Visual Improvements

- Use **consistent headings** and **section dividers** for clarity
- Prefer **tables** for structured data (as above)
- Use **callout boxes** for pro tips, warnings, and expert notes
- Apply a **dark pastel color theme** in your editor for visual comfort
- Add **logos, badges, and icons** for section headers if desired

---

## 11. Next Steps for a “Pretty” Handbook

1. **Copy this Markdown structure** into your favorite editor (Word, Google Docs, Notion, etc.)
2. **Apply styles**:
   - Headings: Use larger, bold fonts for section titles
   - Tables: Use alternating row colors for readability
   - Callouts: Use colored boxes or sidebars for tips and warnings
   - Icons: Add relevant icons to section headers for visual interest
3. **Add a cover page** with the handbook title, version, and a visual theme
4. **Insert a Table of Contents** with clickable links (Word/Google Docs support this)
5. **Review for accessibility**: Use high-contrast colors, clear fonts, and logical heading order

---

## 12. Accessibility & Compliance

- Ensure all images have **alt text**
- Use **semantic headings** (H1, H2, H3, etc.)
- Avoid color-only distinctions—use icons or text labels as well
- Test with screen readers if possible
